Causality and Created Things

Can a Sense Perceive Another Sense's Object?
Baqillani argues for the possibility of sensory crossover via divine creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani affirms the possibility of sensory crossover and how this reflects the Ash'ari principle that God creates all perception directly.

Core Idea
God creates all perception; senses are just occasions.

This passage from Baqillani's Tamhid addresses a subtle theological question: can a sense perceive what normally belongs to another? After affirming the ordinary assignment of senses to objects, he argues that it is possible because perception is directly from God. The following text presents his reasoning and answers a potential objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic once without analysis. Then read the translation. Note the structure: first the customary assignment, then the question, then the answer with proof, then objection and reply.
Pay attention to the phrase 'بمحض خلق الله تعالى'.
2
Identify the key doctrinal move
Baqillani first affirms the ordinary function of senses (hearing for sounds, etc.), then says the truth is permissibility. Why? Because perception is purely from God, not from the sense itself.
This is a classic Ash'ari occasionalist position.
3
Examine the objection and answer
The objection claims taste perceives both sweetness and heat. Baqillani corrects: sweetness is by taste, heat by touch in the mouth. So the senses remain distinct even when co-occurring.
This reinforces that each sense has its own sphere, but God could override it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم بكل حاسة منها أي من الحواس الخمس يوقف أي يطلع على ما وضعت تلك الحاسة له يعني الله تعالى قد خلق كلا من تلك الحواس لإدراك أشياء مخصوصة كالسمع للأصوات والذوق للطعوم والشم للروائح لا يدرك بها ما يدرك بالحاسة الأخرى وأما أنه هل يجوز أو يمتنع ذلك فالحق الجواز لما أن ذلك بمحض خلق الله تعالى من غير تأثير للحواس فلا يمتنع أن يخلق عقيب صرف الباصرة إدراك الأصوات مثلاً فإن قيل أليست الذائقة تدرك حلاوة الشيء وحرارته معاً؟ قلنا : لا بل الحلاوة تدرك بالذوق والحرارة باللمس الموجود في الفم واللسان .
Then, by each sense—meaning each of the five senses—one is informed, i.e., gains knowledge of what that sense is positioned for, meaning that God the Exalted has created each of these senses for the perception of specific things, like hearing for sounds, taste for flavors, smell for odors; what is perceived by one sense is not perceived by another. As for whether that is permissible or impossible, the truth is permissibility, because that is purely by the creation of God the Exalted without any effect of the senses. So it is not impossible that He should create, subsequent to the directing of the sight, the perception of sounds, for example. If it is said: 'Does not the taste faculty perceive the sweetness of a thing and its heat together?' We say: No, rather sweetness is perceived by taste, and heat by touch present in the mouth and tongue.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument about the scope of sensory perception. Baqillani first affirms the customary order: God created each sense for specific objects—hearing for sounds, taste for flavors, smell for odors—and ordinarily a sense does not perceive what belongs to another. Then he addresses the question: could God make a sense perceive what is normally for another? The correct answer (al-ḥaqq) is that it is permissible (jawāz), because perception is purely God's creation, with no effect from the sense itself. Therefore, it is not impossible that God should create the perception of sounds at the moment of directing the sight (i.e., while looking). He then answers an objection: doesn't taste perceive both sweetness and heat? He clarifies that sweetness is perceived by taste, but heat is perceived by touch which exists in the mouth and tongue; it is not that taste perceives heat. This refutes any claim that a sense intrinsically perceives multiple types—rather, when two perceptions occur together, they are via different senses. The argument upholds Ash'ari occasionalism: God creates all perceptions directly, so He is not bound by the ordinary associations of senses and objects.

Key Terms
جواز
خلق الله
إدراك
باصرة
ذائقة
لمس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Senses inherently cause perception of their objects.
Correction: Baqillani teaches that perception is created directly by God; senses are merely occasions.

Checkpoint
Why does Baqillani say it is possible for a sense to perceive what is normally for another sense?
A) Because senses have similar structures
B) Because perception is purely God's creation without the sense's effect
C) Because the senses can learn from each other
D) Because the objection about taste and touch proves it

Key Takeaway
Baqillani upholds that God's power is unrestricted; He can create any perception behind any sense, as perception is His direct creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Baqillani says God could create the perception of sound in your eye at any moment. Are you living today as if your senses are reliable in themselves, or as if every single perception is a direct gift from God that could be changed? What would it mean for you to genuinely depend on Him for the next sound you hear?
?
When you taste something hot and sweet, do you instinctively attribute the experience to the taste buds alone, forgetting that heat is a different sense? How can you train yourself to see the hand of God behind every sensation—even the ordinary ones—starting this afternoon?

Proof for the Existence of Accidents
Rational proof for accidents using motion and rest of the body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof for the existence of accidents based on the body's alternation between motion and rest.

Core Idea
A body's change from motion to rest proves it is not self-moving but caused by an accident.

This passage presents a foundational argument in kalam for the existence of accidents. By observing simple changes in bodies—like motion and rest—the theologian deduces that these changes must be caused by something other than the body itself. That something is an accident. Let's examine this proof step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic text from 'باب الكلام في إثبات الأعراض' up to the cut-off. Notice the argument structure: the body's movement after rest and rest after movement is used as evidence.
The text is incomplete due to OCR; the main argument is still clear.
2
Identify the key premise
The argument states that the body's change must be either by itself or by a cause. If it were self-moving, it could never rest. Since it does rest, its motion is caused by something else.
3
Extend the proof to other accidents
The same reasoning applies to colors, tastes, smells, and other qualities. The body's possession of any changing attribute indicates an accident as the cause.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes (though incomplete) that the body is never without an accident, and it is impossible for it to be self-moving. This establishes the necessity of accidents as the cause of all change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام في إثبات الأعراض
والدليل على إثبات الأعراض تحرُّكُ الجسم بعد سكونه وسكونه بعد حركته، ولا بد أن يكون ذلك كذلك لنفسه أو لعلّة، فلو كان متحركاً لنفسه ما جاز سكونه، وفي صحة سكونه بعد تحركه دليل على أنه متحرك لعلّة هي الحركة. وهذا الدليل هو الدليل على إثبات الألوان والطعوم والأرابيح والتأليف والحياة والموت والعلم والجهل والقدرة والعجز وغير ذلك من ضروبها. ويدل على ذلك أن الجسم لا يخلو من لمعنى، ويستحيل أن يكون متحركاً لنفسه لأن ذلك لو كان كذلك لوجب أن يكون متحركاً لنفسه أو
Chapter on speech about proving accidents. The proof for the existence of accidents is the body's movement after its rest and its rest after its movement. It must be that it is like that either by itself or by a cause. If it were moving by itself, its rest would not be possible. And the validity of its rest after its movement is evidence that it is moving by a cause, which is movement. This proof is the proof for establishing colors, tastes, smells, composition, life, death, knowledge, ignorance, power, inability, and other kinds of them. And it also indicates that the body is not devoid of a meaning (accident), and it is impossible for it to be moving by itself because if that were so, it would necessarily...
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage provides a rational proof for the existence of accidents. The author argues from the body's alternation between motion and rest: if the body were self-moving, it could not rest; but since it does rest, its motion must be caused by something other than itself—that cause is the accident of movement. The same reasoning applies to all other accidents like colors, tastes, etc. The argument then adds that a body is never devoid of a 'meaning' (accident), and it cannot be self-moving, concluding (though incomplete) that accidents must exist as the cause of change. This is a classic kalam argument for the existence of accidents based on observable change.

Key Terms

علة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the argument proves only the accident of motion, not other accidents.
Correction: The author explicitly states that this same proof establishes colors, tastes, smells, and all other accidents, as they are similar kinds of change.

Checkpoint
What is the main proof for the existence of accidents given in this passage?
A) The composition of bodies
B) The alternation of motion and rest
C) The definition of substance
D) The Quranic verses

Key Takeaway
A body's change from motion to rest demonstrates it is not self-sufficient; it requires an accident as the cause of change.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your body moves and rests without your conscious control – when was the last time you thanked Allah for the accidents that keep you alive? Do you take them for granted?
?
You often blame your bad mood or illness on external factors, but do you realize that every single change in your body is an accident created directly by Allah? How does that change your perspective on your daily struggles?
?
Are you living as if your own will is the cause of your actions, or do you truly believe that every motion, every breath, is an accident sustained by Allah? What would change in your life if you lived with that conviction starting today?

Proof of Accidents from Motion and Rest
Baqillani proves the existence of accidents using the observation of motion and rest.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the observation of motion and rest to prove the existence of accidents and why motion cannot be inherent in bodies.

Core Idea
Motion and rest in bodies reveal that accidents are real and caused.

Baqillani begins by establishing a fundamental proof for the existence of accidents—those transient attributes that inhere in substances. By observing simple changes like a body moving after being still, he demonstrates that such changes cannot come from the body's own nature and must therefore be caused by something else: the accident of movement. This argument becomes a template for proving all accidents.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once. Notice the structure: observation, dilemma, conclusion.
Pay attention to the logical flow.
2
Identify the core proof
Find the sentence: 'the body's movement after its rest and its rest after its movement.' Understand why this is a proof.
3
Understand the dilemma
The body's movement must be either from itself or from a cause. Baqillani eliminates the first option. What is the reasoning?
If movement were from itself, rest would be impossible.
4
See the extension
How does this same proof apply to other accidents like colors, tastes, etc.? Notice the list.
5
Reflect on the argument from kind
Why would a body moving by itself require all similar bodies to be moving? How does this confirm the proof?
This strengthens the case that movement is caused.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام في إثبات الأعراض والدليل على إثبات الأعراض تحرك الجسم بعد سكونه وسكونه بعد حركته ولا بد أن يكون ذلك كذلك لنفسه أو لعلة، فلو كان متحركا لنفسه ما جاز سكونه، وفي صحة سكونه بعد تحركه دليل على أنه متحرك لعلة هي الحركة. وهذا الدليل هو الدليل على إثبات الألوان والطعوم والأرابيح والتأليف والحياة والموت والعلم والجهل والقدرة والعجز وغير ذلك من ضروبها. ويدل على ذلك أن الجسم لا يخلو من معنى، ويستحيل أن يكون متحركا لنفسه لأن ذلك لو كان كذلك لوجب أن لا يوجد من جنسه في ذلك الوقت إلا ما كان متحركا، ألا ترى أن السواد إذا كان سوادا لنفسه لم يجز أن يوجد من جنسه ما ليس بسواد؟ وفي العلم بأنه قد يوجد من جنس الجواهر والأجسام المتحركة ما ليس بمتحرك دليل على أن المتحرك فيها ليس بمتحرك لنفسه وأنه للحركة كان متحركا.
Chapter on speech concerning the proof of accidents. And the proof for the existence of accidents is the body's movement after its rest and its rest after its movement. And it is necessary that this be so either from itself or from a cause. For if it were moving from itself, its rest would not be possible. And in the validity of its rest after its movement is a proof that it moves due to a cause, which is movement (al-ḥaraka). And this proof is the proof for the existence of colors, tastes, smells, composition, life, death, knowledge, ignorance, power, incapacity, and other types of them. And that is indicated by the fact that the body is not free from a meaning, and it is impossible for it to be moving from itself, because if that were the case, then it would be necessary that nothing of its kind exists at that time except what is moving. Do you not see that if blackness were black from itself, it would not be possible for something of its kind that is not black to exist? And in the knowledge that there may exist among the kind of substances and moving bodies what is not moving, there is proof that the moving thing among them is not moving from itself, and that it moves due to movement (al-ḥaraka).
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage provides a proof for the existence of accidents (a'raad). Baqillani argues that a body can be observed to move after being still and to be still after moving. This change cannot be due to the body's own nature, because if it were inherently moving, it could not rest. Since rest does occur, the movement must be caused by something else, which is the accident of movement (ḥaraka). This same proof also establishes other accidents like colors, tastes, smells, etc., because they too are impermanent. He then strengthens the argument by noting that if a body moved by itself, all bodies of its kind would always be moving, but we find stationary bodies among moving substances. Therefore, movement must be due to an external cause, i.e., the accident of movement.

Key Terms
تحرك
سكون
علة
حركة
نفس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Motion is an inherent property of bodies; bodies are naturally moving or at rest by themselves.
Correction: Baqillani demonstrates that motion cannot be inherent because the same body can be both moving and at rest at different times. If motion were inherent, rest would be impossible. Therefore, motion must be caused by an external accident.

Checkpoint
What is the main evidence Baqillani uses to prove the existence of accidents?
A) Revelation.
B) The body's rest and movement.
C) The body's color.
D) Consensus.

Key Takeaway
The observation that a body can move after being still proves that motion is not inherent but caused by the accident of movement, establishing the reality of accidents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that your body's motion and rest are not from your essence but from accidents that come and go. What about the 'movements' of your heart—your desires, fears, or attachments? Do you treat them as fixed parts of who you are, or as accidents that can change? Will you examine one attachment today and ask whether it is from a cause you can address?
?
Baqillani argues that if motion were essential, no body could ever rest. Think of a habit you consider unchangeable—maybe procrastination in prayer or an addiction. If that habit were truly essential, you could never stop. But you have experienced moments of rest from it. Does that not prove it is accidental? What cause might be sustaining it, and are you willing to remove that cause?
?
The proof extends to knowledge and ignorance: they are accidents, not essential. Consider a belief you hold to be absolute truth. If that belief were essential to your soul, you could never doubt or question it. But you have doubted. So it is not essential. What then is the cause of your belief? Is it the truth itself, or something else? Will you seek the cause that makes your belief true?

Motion is not self-subsistent: an analogy
Baqillani proves motion is not self-subsistent using the analogy of blackness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani uses the analogy of blackness to demonstrate that motion is not an essential property of bodies but an accident caused by an external agent.

Core Idea
Motion is not essential to bodies; it is an accidental property requiring an external cause.

This short passage from Baqillani's Tamhid presents a concise logical argument. Using the example of blackness, he shows that if motion were self-subsistent, all bodies would always be moving, which contradicts our observations. This lesson unpacks the analogy and its implications for causality in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Pay attention to the key terms: al-mutaharrik (the moving), as-sawad (blackness), bidhdhat (by itself/essence), bil-'arad (accidentally).
The passage is short but dense.
2
Understand the analogy
Notice the rhetorical question about blackness: if blackness is black by itself, can there be a non-black member of its genus? The answer is no. This sets up the standard for self-subsistent properties.
This is a key logical move.
3
Apply the analogy to motion
Baqillani then applies the same logic: among bodies, we find both moving and non-moving examples. Therefore, motion cannot be self-subsistent like blackness. It must be accidental.
This shows motion is caused.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that the mover (the moving body) is not moving by itself but 'by motion was moving'. This underscores the need for a cause of motion.
This is a foundational principle for proving the existence of Allah as the mover.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يوجد من جنسه في ذلك الوقت إلا ما كان متحركاً، ألا ترى أن السواد إذا كان سواداً لنفسه لم يجز أن يوجد من جنسه ما ليس بسواد؟ وفي العلم بأنه قد يوجد من جنس الجواهر والأجسام المتحركة ما ليس بمتحرك دليل على أن المتحرك فيها ليس بمتحرك لنفسه وأنه للحركة كان متحركاً.
There does not exist from its genus at that time except what was moving. Do you not see that blackness, if it is blackness by itself, it is not permissible that there exist from its genus what is not black? And in the knowledge that there may exist from the genus of substances and moving bodies what is not moving, there is evidence that the mover among them is not moving by itself, and that by motion it was moving.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage presents an analogy to prove that motion in bodies is not self-subsistent (i.e., not an essential attribute of the body itself). The author argues: If motion were self-subsistent, then it would be impossible to find a member of the same genus (i.e., bodies) that is not moving, just as blackness, if it is black by its own essence, cannot have a member of its genus that is not black. But we observe that among substances and moving bodies, there are some that are not moving at a given time. This shows that motion is not an essential property of the body; rather, the body becomes moving through motion (an accident). Hence, motion is caused by an external agent.

Key Terms
المتحرك
السواد
بالذات
بالعرض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Motion is an inherent and essential property of bodies; bodies move by their own nature.
Correction: Baqillani shows that if motion were essential, all bodies would always move, but we observe stationary bodies. Therefore motion is accidental and requires an external cause.

Checkpoint
What does the example of blackness illustrate about motion?
A) Motion is inherent to bodies.
B) Motion is not essential but accidental to bodies.
C) Blackness and motion are equivalent.
D) Bodies are essentially moving.

Key Takeaway
Motion is not an essential property of bodies; it is an accident that requires a cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever act as if your own movements—your walking, your speech, your breath—are self-generated, forgetting that every motion is an accident sustained by Allah? How can you turn your next step into a conscious acknowledgement of His constant provision?
?
If motion is a contingent accident, then your very existence from moment to moment is utterly dependent on Allah. What would change in your daily life if you truly believed that you cannot even lift a finger without His permission? Will you make a specific dua today asking Him to keep you moving towards what pleases Him?
?
The blackness analogy shows that a self-subsistent property leaves no room for its absence. But you are not self-subsistent; you are needy and changeable. How does this humbling truth affect the way you approach Allah in your prayers? Will you spend one minute in sujood silently acknowledging that every part of your body is a gift and a sign of His power?

Six Possible Objects of God's Power Over Motion
Baqillani lists six possible objects of power for moving a body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the six logical possibilities for what God's power to move a body applies to, as enumerated by Imam Baqillani.

Core Idea
God's power over motion has six possible objects; only one can be correct.

Imam Baqillani begins by observing that human power over motion varies, implying that power always has a real object (maqdur). He then applies this to God's power to move a body, listing six possibilities for what that object could be. Understanding these options is crucial for the subsequent arguments in kalam about how God acts in the world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the human analogy
Start by reading the Arabic and translation. Notice how Baqillani uses the variability of human power to establish that power must have an object of power (maqdur).
The human case is used as evidence (dalil) for divine power.
2
Identify the six enumerated possibilities
After stating the principle, Baqillani lists six options for what the object of God's power over moving a body could be. Try to list them yourself before reading the commentary.
The list is given in a single long sentence: 'إما أن يكون... أو...'.
3
Understand the last two ambiguous options
The fifth and sixth options are phrased negatively: 'or not for itself and not for a meaning connected to itself'. The commentary explains this likely means the power has no real object, or that the object is the body itself without any accident.
These are refuted in later passages.
4
Ask why this enumeration matters
Reflect on why Baqillani spends time listing possibilities that he will later refute. This is a standard dialectical method: exhaust the alternatives to show that only one is correct.
This leads to the conclusion that God's power to move a body is over producing an accident (meaning) in it, not over the body itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يدل على ذلك عِلمنا بأن الإنسان تارة يقدر على التحرك ويعجز عنه أخرى وقد ثبت أنه لا بدّ لقدرته من تعلّق بمقدور، وكذلك القديم تعالى يقدر عند الموحدين وعند من أثبته من الملحدين النافين للأعراض على تحريك الجسم تارة وعلى تسكينه أخرى فلا يخلو أن يكون مقدورُ القدرة على تحريك الجسم هو إحداث الجسم وإيجاده أو إحداث معنى فيه أو إعدامه أو إعدام معنى منه أو لا لنفسه أو لمعنى تعلق بنفسه.
And among the things that indicate that is our knowledge that a man sometimes has power to move and is unable at other times, and it has been established that his power must have a connection to an object of power (maqdur). And likewise, the Eternal (al-Qadim), Exalted is He, has power (according to the monotheists and according to those who affirm Him among the atheists who deny accidents) to move a body sometimes and to still it at other times. So it is not free from that the object of power of the power over moving the body is either the origination (ihdath) of the body and its bringing into existence, or the origination of a meaning (ma'na) in it, or its annihilation, or the annihilation of a meaning from it, or not for itself and not for a meaning connected to itself.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage introduces the problem of what the power (qudra) to move a body actually applies to. The author observes that human power over motion is variable (sometimes able, sometimes unable), so it must have a real object (maqdur). Similarly, God's power to move or still a body must have a maqdur. The author then enumerates the logical possibilities: (1) the maqdur is the creation of the body itself (i.e., the act of moving is actually creating the body anew), (2) the maqdur is the creation of a meaning (accident) in the body, (3) the maqdur is the annihilation of the body, (4) the maqdur is the annihilation of a meaning from the body, (5) the maqdur is nothing at all (neither body nor meaning), or (6) the maqdur is the body itself without any meaning. Note: the last option 'or not for itself and not for a meaning connected to itself' is ambiguous; it likely refers to the possibility that the power has no real object. The subsequent passages refute these alternatives.

Key Terms
القدرة
المقدور
الإحداث
الإعدام
المعنى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the power to move a body is directly over the body itself without any additional object.
Correction: Baqillani shows that this is only one of six possibilities, and it will be refuted in subsequent passages.

Checkpoint
How many possible objects of power (maqdur) does the author list for moving a body?
A) Four
B) Five
C) Six
D) Three

Key Takeaway
Baqillani enumerates six logical possibilities for what God's power to move a body could apply to, setting the stage for later refutation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you move your hand intentionally, do you ever pause to recognize that God's power is the ultimate cause of that movement? How would your awareness of this change your moment-by-moment reliance on Him?
?
Baqillani argues that power must be tied to a specific object. Is there an area of your life where you claim to have power, but you resist naming the exact object of that power? What would it mean to be honest about what you can and cannot control?
?
The passage lists many possibilities for what God's power could apply to, but the truth is only one. Are you willing to seek that truth even if it requires you to reject comfortable assumptions about how the world works? What assumption are you most attached to that this lesson challenges?

Causality and Created Things
beginner
5 min
Refutation: The Object of Power Is Not the Creation of the Body
Baqillani refutes that the maqdur for motion is the creation of the body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani argues that the object of power (maqdur) when moving a body cannot be the creation of the body itself.

Core Idea
A power must have a distinct object; motion is not re-creation.

In this passage, Baqillani presents a crucial refutation within his argument about divine power and motion. He has already established that a power (qudra) must have an object (maqdur). Now he considers a potential misunderstanding: that the maqdur for moving a body is the creation of the body itself. He shows why this is impossible, using both analogy and logical reasoning. Understanding this refutation clarifies the relationship between power, motion, and the temporality of bodies.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main claim
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice that Baqillani is rejecting the idea that the object of power for motion is the creation of the body. He gives two reasons.
The first reason is analogical, the second is direct.
2
Understand the analogy with knowledge and mention
Baqillani says that just as knowledge must have an object (known) and mention must have an object (mentioned), so power must have an object. This establishes that power cannot be without a maqdur.
Think about why this analogy supports the refutation.
3
Analyze the direct refutation
The body moves in the second moment of its existence, while its creation (origination) occurred in the first moment. Therefore, motion cannot be identical to creation. If it were, the body would be created again, which is not the case.
Consider the temporal sequence: creation happens at the beginning, motion happens later.
4
Consider the consequence if it were true
Baqillani notes that if motion were creation, then that would actually prove the body's temporality (huduth), which is the desired conclusion. However, the premise is false, so the argument stands as a refutation of this specific claim.
This shows that not all arguments that lead to a true conclusion are valid; the premises must be sound.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستحيل أن تكون القدرة على ذلك لا تعلق لها بمقدور كما يستحيل وجود علم لا تعلق له بمعلوم وذكر لا تعلق له بمذكور. ويستحيل أن يكون مقدورُ القدرة هو إيجاد الجسم وإحداثه لأنه إنما يتحرك في الثاني من حال وجوده مع استحالة حدوثه وتجدّده في ذلك الوقت ولأن ذلك إن كان كذلك فقد صح وثبت حدوث الجسم وهذا هو الذي نبتغيه بإثبات الأعراض.
And it is impossible for the power over that to have no connection to an object of power, just as it is impossible for knowledge to exist without a connection to a known, and mention without a connection to a mentioned. And it is impossible that the object of power of the power is the bringing into existence (ijad) of the body and its origination (ihdath), because it (the body) only moves in the second [moment] from the state of its existence, with the impossibility of its origination and renewal at that time. And because if that were so, then the temporality (huduth) of the body would be established and confirmed, and this is what we seek by affirming accidents (a'rad).
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage refutes the first possibility: that the maqdur (object of power) when moving a body is the creation of the body itself. The author gives two reasons. First, a power must have a real object; it cannot be without a maqdur, just as knowledge requires a known. Second, the body moves in the second moment of its existence, i.e., after it already exists. If movement were the same as creating the body, then movement would be identical to origination, which is impossible because the body is already existing when it moves. Moreover, if movement were creation, then this would prove that the body is temporal (created in time), which is exactly what the author wants to establish by proving accidents. However, the refutation is that this option leads to a contradiction because movement is not the same as origination.

Key Terms

الإيجاد
الإحداث
الحدوث
الأعراض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The object of power when moving a body is the creation of the body itself.
Correction: The author shows this is impossible because the body moves after it exists, and creation is not repeated. Power must have a distinct object.

Checkpoint
Why cannot the object of power for moving a body be the creation of the body?
A) Because creation is impossible for God
B) Because the body moves after it exists, and creation is not repeated
C) Because motion is an accident
D) Because the body is eternal

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the idea that moving a body is equivalent to creating it, using the necessity of a maqdur and the temporal sequence of motion.

?
The author argues that power cannot exist without an object. Is there any area of your life where you act without a clear purpose or object? How can you align your actions with the knowledge that every power has a maqdur?
?
Reflect on the concept of 'renewal' (tajaddud) in your own life. Are you constantly trying to recreate yourself instead of recognizing the one-time creation by God? How can you accept God's creation of you and still seek improvement?

4 min
Annihilation is Not a Created Thing
First refutation: annihilation is not an object of power

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why non-existence (annihilation) cannot be the object of divine power because it is not a created or acquired thing.

Core Idea
Power cannot attach to non-existence because non-existence is not a thing that occurs.

In this passage, Baqillani refutes the claim that the object of power is the annihilation of a meaning from the body. He first argues that annihilation is not a positive entity; it is a negation. Since power only attaches to things that come into existence or are acquired, it cannot attach to mere absence. This is a foundational principle in Sunni kalam about the nature of divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and its translation to understand the flow of the argument.
Pay attention to the key terms like إعدام and عدم.
2
Identify the two possibilities
Notice that the meaning annihilated is either a body or an accident. Consider how each case supports the author's position.
The author uses the opponent's own concessions.
3
Grasp the core refutation
Understand that non-existence is not a created or acquired thing, so power cannot be connected to it.
This is the pivotal point of the first argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قيل يستحيل أن يكون مقدور القدرة إعدام معنى من الجسم لأن ذلك المعنى لا يخلو أن يكون جسماً أو عرضاً فإن كان جسماً أقروا بجواز عدم الجسم وصح بذلك حدوثه لاستحالة عدم القديم عندنا وعندهم وذلك ما أردناه وإن كان عرضاً فقد أقروا بوجود الأعراض وعدمها بعد الوجود وهذا ما رمنا إثباته ولأن عدم معنى من الجسم ليس بشيء يحدث ولا يُكتسب فمُحالٌ تعلُّق القدرة بما ليس بمعنى يحدث ويكتسب فبطل هذا القول. ولأن الجسم لو تحرك في جهة بعينها وإلى محاذاة بعينها لعدم معنى منه مع صحة تحركه مع عدم ذلك المعنى إلى غير تلك الجهة والمحاذاة لم يكن بأن يتحرك إلى الجهة والمحاذاة التي تحرك إليها أولى من تحركه إلى غيرها؛ وفي العلم بكونه أولى بالتحرك إلى ما تحرك إليه وأحق به في ذلك الوقت دليل على بطلان هذا القول. ولأن الجسم أيضاً لو تحرك لعدم معنى منه لم يكن هو بالتحرك أولى من غيره من الأجسام لأن ذلك المعنى الذي عُدِم منه ليس هو فيه ولا في غيره؛ فيجب لذلك تحرك كل ما ليس فيه ذلك المعنى وفي العلم ببطلان هذا دليل على فساد هذا القول.
And if it is said: It is impossible that the object of power of the power is the annihilation ('adam) of a meaning from the body, because that meaning is not free from being either a body or an accident. If it is a body, they affirm the possibility of the non-existence of the body, and thereby its temporality is established, due to the impossibility of the non-existence of the Eternal according to us and them, and that is what we intended. If it is an accident, they affirm the existence of accidents and their non-existence after existence, and this is what we seek to establish. And because the non-existence of a meaning from the body is not a thing that occurs (yahduth) nor is acquired (yuktasab), so the connection of power to what is not a meaning that occurs or is acquired is impossible. So this statement is nullified. And because if the body moved in a specific direction and to a specific alignment due to the absence of a meaning from it, while it is possible for it to move with the absence of that meaning to another direction and alignment, it would not be more deserving of moving to the direction and alignment to which it moved than to moving to others; and in the knowledge that it is more deserving of moving to what it moved to and more entitled to it at that time is evidence of the nullity of this statement. And because if the body moved due to the absence of a meaning from it, it would not be more deserving of moving than other bodies, because that meaning which was absent from it is not present in it nor in others; so therefore every body that does not possess that meaning would have to move, and in the knowledge of the nullity of this is evidence of the corruption of this statement.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage refutes the possibility that the maqdur for moving a body is the annihilation of a meaning (accident) from the body. The author gives several arguments. First, the meaning that is annihilated must be either a body or an accident. If it is a body, annihilation implies the body's temporality, which the author accepts. If it is an accident, annihilation exists, which also supports the author's thesis. However, the real objection is that non-existence (absence) is not a created or acquired thing; it is a negation. Therefore, power cannot attach to it. Second, if motion were due to the absence of a specific meaning, then the body should be equally likely to move in any direction when that meaning is absent, but we observe it moves in a particular direction preferentially. This shows that the cause is not mere absence but a positive accident (motion). Third, if motion were due to absence, then any body lacking that meaning would have to move, but we observe bodies with the same absence not moving. Thus, the idea is refuted.

المعنى
العدم
الجهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that annihilation (causing non-existence) is an act of power like creating.
Correction: Non-existence is not a created thing; power only attaches to positive entities that come into existence.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason Baqillani rejects that annihilation is the object of power?
A) Annihilation is impossible
B) Non-existence is not a created thing
C) The meaning is always a body
D) Accidents are not real

Key Takeaway
Non-existence is not a created entity, so power cannot directly cause it.

Directional Preference Shows a Positive Cause
Second refutation: directional preference contradicts absence as cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why motion cannot be due to annihilation of a meaning, because if annihilation were the cause, the body would have no reason to move in one direction over another.

Core Idea
If motion were due to absence, the body would be equally likely to move anywhere.

Baqillani provides a second powerful argument. If a body's motion were caused by the absence of a certain meaning, then whenever that meaning is absent, the body should be equally likely to move in any direction. But we observe that bodies move in specific directions at specific times, indicating a positive cause (like an accidental quality of motion) rather than mere absence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the second argument carefully, noting the conditional structure.
2
Grasp the conditional reasoning
Understand that if motion were due to absence, then with the same absence, the body could move in any direction equally.
The absence is the same regardless of direction.
3
Recognize the empirical refutation
We observe that the body moves in a specific direction, which cannot be explained by a uniform absence.
This shows there must be a positive cause.

Absence Would Cause All Bodies to Move
Third refutation: absence would necessitate universal motion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that if motion were due to annihilation of a meaning, then any body lacking that meaning would have to move, which is false.

Core Idea
If absence causes motion, all bodies lacking that meaning would move equally.

Baqillani's third argument is a proof from universalizability. If a body's motion were caused by the absence of a specific meaning, then any other body that also lacks that meaning should also move. But we observe many bodies that lack the same meaning yet do not move. This contradiction refutes the claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the third argument, which is a reductio ad absurdum.
2
Understand the universal implication
If the absence of meaning M causes motion in body A, then any body lacking M should also move.
Because the cause (absence) is present in all such bodies.
3
Recognize the empirical contradiction
We see bodies lacking M that do not move, so the cause cannot be absence.
This shows the claim is false.

Proof for the Existence of Accidents
Baqillani proves that motion requires an accident, refuting alternatives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's rational proof that motion in bodies is caused by created accidents, and why alternative explanations fail.

Core Idea
Motion cannot be explained by absence; it requires a real, caused meaning.

Imam al-Baqillani, a master of the Ash'ari school, presents a rigorous demonstration that accidents exist. He argues that when a body moves, something new must come into being—an accident—which is the object of God's power. In this passage, he systematically refutes the idea that motion could be due to the non-existence of a quality, showing that such absence cannot be a cause. Follow along as he builds his case step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the full argument
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get the overall flow. Notice how Baqillani uses multiple 'because' ('ولأن') statements.
This is a dense text; don't worry about every detail yet.
2
Identify the first refutation
Find where Baqillani rejects the idea that motion is due to the non-existence of a meaning. What is his main objection?
He says non-existence is not a thing that occurs or is acquired.
3
Follow the second and third refutations
Notice the arguments about direction and universal motion. How does he prove that absence cannot explain why a body moves one way rather than another?
4
Understand the positive conclusion
After refuting alternatives, Baqillani states his positive claim: the power to move a body is power to create an accident in it.
This is the core of the proof.
5
Consider the additional support
He adds arguments about human power and the meaninglessness of 'moving' without a cause. Why are these points necessary?
They reinforce the necessity of accidents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما أردناه وإن كان عرضاً فقد أقروا بوجود الأعراض وعدمها بعد الوجود وهذا ما رمنا إثباته ولأن عدم معنى من الجسم ليس بشيء يحدث ولا يكتسب فمحال تعلق القدرة بما ليس بمعنى يحدث ويكتسب فبطل هذا القول. ولأن الجسم لو تحرك في جهة بعينها وإلى محاذاة بعينها لعدم معنى منه مع صحة تحركه مع عدم ذلك المعنى إلى غير تلك الجهة والمحاذاة لم يكن بأن يتحرك إلى الجهة والمحاذاة التي تحرك إليها أولى من تحركه إلى غيرها؛ وفي العلم بكونه أولى بالتحرك إلى ما تحرك إليه وأحق به في ذلك الوقت دليل على بطلان هذا القول. ولأن الجسم أيضاً لو تحرك لعدم معنى منه لم يكن هو بالتحرك أولى من غيره من الأجسام لأن ذلك المعنى الذي عدم منه ليس هو فيه ولا في غيره؛ فيجب لذلك تحرك كل ما ليس فيه ذلك المعنى وفي العلم ببطلان هذا دليل على فساد هذا القول. ويستحيل أيضاً أن يكون مقدور القدرة على تحريك الجسم ما ليس هو نفس الجسم ولا معنى سواه؛ لأن ما ليس هو نفسه ولا معنى غيره ليس بشيء أن يكون حادثاً أو مكتسباً فبطل أيضاً هذا الوجه وصح بذلك أن قدرة القادر على تحريك الجسم قدرة على فعل معنى فيه أو اكتسابه، وهذا هو معنى قولنا إن المتحرك كان متحركاً بالفاعل. ويدل على أن قدرة الإنسان على المتحرك لا يجوز أن تكون قدرة على نفسه علمنا وهم باستحالة كون الإنسان فاعلاً للأجسام وأنه لو صح ذلك وأن يقدر على نفسه لصح أن يقدر على مثله، ومما يدل أيضاً على أنه لا يجوز أن يكون المتحرك متحركاً لا لنفسه ولا لعلة أن ذلك لو كان كذلك لصار قولنا فيه إنه متحرك لقباً لا فائدة تحته ولجرى مجرى تسميتنا زيداً زيداً وذلك باطل ولأن ذلك لو كان كذلك لم يكن هو بالتحرك أولى من غيره ولخرج قولنا: متحرك عن أن يكون له مثبتاً ومخبراً عنه وإن كان إثباتاً وخبراً لأنه غير راجع إلى نفس الجسم ولا إلى معنى سواه وذلك باطل باتفاق وهذا يحيل أن يكون شيء من الأوصاف مستحقاً لا لنفس ولا لعلة، وفي بعض ما أومأنا إليه دليل على إثبات الأعراض.
What we intended, and even if it is an accident, they have acknowledged the existence of accidents and their non-existence after existence, and this is what we sought to prove. And because the non-existence of a meaning from the body is not a thing that occurs or is acquired, so it is impossible for power to attach to what is not a meaning that occurs and is acquired, so this statement is invalid. And because if the body moved in a specific direction and to a specific alignment due to the non-existence of a meaning from it, while it is possible for it to move without that meaning to another direction and alignment, it would not be more deserving of moving to the direction and alignment to which it moved than moving to others; and in the knowledge of its being more deserving of moving to what it moved to and more entitled to it at that time is evidence of the invalidity of this statement. And because also if the body moved due to the non-existence of a meaning from it, it would not be more deserving of moving than other bodies, because that meaning which is absent from it is not in it nor in others; therefore it would be necessary for everything in which that meaning is not present to move, and in the knowledge of the invalidity of this is evidence of the corruption of this statement. And it is also impossible for what is in the power of the powerful to move the body to be something that is neither the body itself nor a meaning other than it; because what is neither itself nor another meaning is nothing that occurs or is acquired, so this aspect also is invalid, and thus it is established that the power of the powerful over moving the body is a power to effect a meaning in it or acquire it, and this is the meaning of our statement that the moving thing was moving by the agent. And it indicates that the power of man over the moving thing cannot be a power over himself, our knowledge and theirs of the impossibility of man being an agent of bodies, and that if that were valid and that he were able over himself, it would be valid for him to be able over the like of him. And among what also indicates that the moving thing cannot be moving neither by itself nor by a cause is that if that were the case, our statement about it that it is moving would become a label with no benefit under it, and it would run the course of our naming Zayd as Zayd, and that is false. And because if that were the case, it would not be more deserving of moving than others, and our statement 'moving' would depart from being an established and reported thing, even if it is an establishment and a report, because it does not refer back to the body itself nor to a meaning other than it, and that is false by consensus. And this renders impossible that any attribute be merited neither by itself nor by a cause. And in some of what we hinted at is evidence for the establishment of accidents.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a multi-step proof for the existence of accidents (a'rāḍ). The author, Imam al-Baqillani, argues that motion in a body cannot be explained without positing an accident (ma'nā) that is created by the agent. He refutes alternative views: (1) If motion were due to the absence of a meaning, that absence is not a real thing that occurs, so power cannot attach to it. (2) If motion were due to absence, the body would have no reason to move in one direction rather than another, leading to contradiction. (3) If motion were due to absence, all bodies lacking that meaning would have to move, which is false. (4) It is impossible for the object of power to be neither the body nor an accident, because that is nothing. Therefore, the power to move a body is the power to create an accident in it. He then provides additional support: human power cannot be over one's own body because man cannot create bodies, and if motion were not due to a cause, the term 'moving' would be a meaningless label. The conclusion is that accidents must exist.

Key Terms
عرض (accident)
معنى (meaning)
قدرة (power)
متحرك (moving)
فاعل (agent)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think motion could be caused by the absence of a quality, similar to how something becomes hot when coldness is removed.
Correction: Baqillani shows that absence is not a real thing that can be an object of power or a cause of motion, as it leads to contradictions like universal motion and lack of specific direction.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is it impossible for the power of the agent to attach to the non-existence of a meaning from the body?
A) Because non-existence is a thing that occurs and is acquired.
B) Because non-existence is not a thing that occurs or is acquired.
C) Because non-existence is the same as the body.
D) Because non-existence is a meaning.

Key Takeaway
Accidents are real entities created by God, and motion cannot be explained by mere absence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you move your hand to read this, did you consider that motion as a created accident dependent on God every moment? How would your awareness of His constant creation change your daily actions?
?
If motion without a cause is a meaningless label, what does that say about your life if you attribute your actions to mere habit or chance rather than to the Creator's ongoing act? Are you willing to see every movement as a sign of His power?
?
Baqillani argues that if motion were due to absence, there would be no reason to prefer one direction. Look at your own choices today—do you act as if there is no real cause behind your preferences, or do you acknowledge that every inclination is created by Allah? What would it mean to submit even your preferences to Him?

Classification of the World and Proof of Accidents' Temporality
Baqillani classifies the world into substances and accidents and proves accidents are temporal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's classification of the world into substances and accidents and his proof that accidents are temporal.

Core Idea
The world is entirely temporal, proven by the impossibility of motion and rest coexisting.

In this passage, Imam Baqillani lays the foundation for arguing that the entire world is created (muḥdath) by first dividing it into its fundamental categories: substances and accidents. Then he provides a clear, intuitive proof that accidents are temporal, using the contradictory states of motion and rest. Understanding this proof is essential for grasping the broader kalām cosmological argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise and logical style of Baqillani.
2
Identify the two categories
The passage states that the entire world consists of two genera: substances (jawāhir) and accidents (aʿrāḍ). Make sure you understand these terms.
Substances are self-subsisting entities; accidents are attributes that inhere in substances.
3
Follow the proof for accidents' temporality
Baqillani argues that motion must cease when rest arrives, otherwise both would coexist—an impossibility. Walk through each step of this argument.
This is a classic example of a proof by contradiction in kalām.
4
Connect to the bigger picture
The proof that accidents are temporal is used to prove that the entire world is temporal, since the world comprises substances and accidents.
The full cosmological argument is built on this foundation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام في إثبات حدث العالم
جميع العالم العلوي والسفلي لا يخرج عن هذين الجنسين؛ أعني الجواهر والأعراض وهو محدث بأسره والدليل على حدثه ما قدمناه من إثبات الأعراض.
والأعراض حوادث والدليل على حدوثها بطلان الحركة عند مجيء السكون لأنها لو لم تبطل عند مجيء السكون لكانا موجودين في الجسم معاً ولوجب لذلك أن يكون متحركاً ساكناً معاً وذلك مما يعلم فساده ضرورة.
Chapter on proving the creation of the world. All the higher and lower world does not exceed these two genera: namely, substances and accidents, and it is entirely created. The proof of its creation is what we have presented of the proof of accidents. Accidents are temporal occurrences, and the proof of their temporality is the cessation of motion when rest arrives, because if it did not cease when rest arrives, both would exist together in the body, and it would be necessary that it be both moving and restful at the same time, and that is known to be false by necessity.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage defines the world's composition into two categories: substances (jawāhir) and accidents (aʿrāḍ), and asserts that the entire world is temporally originated (muḥdath). The proof for the temporality of the world is based on the prior proof of the temporality of accidents. Then, it directly proves that accidents are temporal using a simple observation: motion and rest cannot coexist in a body simultaneously. If motion did not cease when rest arrives, the body would have to be both moving and still at the same time, which is impossible. Therefore, motion must be a temporal accident that comes and goes, proving its originated nature.

Key Terms
جواهر
أعراض
حدث
بطلان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the argument relies on motion and rest being opposites that cannot coexist, but it is actually about the impossibility of a body being described by two contradictory states simultaneously.
Correction: The argument is not merely about opposites; it is a logical proof that an accident like motion cannot persist when its opposite (rest) arrives, leading to a contradiction.

Checkpoint
What is the basis for proving that accidents are temporal?
A) The body cannot exist without accidents
B) Motion and rest cannot coexist in a body at the same time
C) The world is composed of substances and accidents
D) The philosophers denied the temporality of accidents

Key Takeaway
The temporality of the world is proven by the temporality of accidents, which is demonstrated by the impossibility of motion and rest coexisting in a body.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Baqillani argues that the world is entirely temporal—nothing in it is permanent. Your own body, your health, your wealth, your relationships—all are a collection of changing accidents. If you truly believed this moment that none of these will last, what would you do differently today? Name one specific thing you will begin or stop doing as a direct result.
?
The proof that motion and rest cannot coexist is 'known to be false by necessity.' Yet in your heart, you often try to hold contradictory states: wanting both the world and the Hereafter, seeking both praise from people and sincerity for Allah. Identify one area where you are trying to keep motion and rest together. What is the first step you will take tonight to let go of one?
?
If this world is temporary and created, then your ultimate home is with the Creator. What attachment in your life—a possession, a status, a relationship—do you cling to as if it were eternal? How will you remind yourself of its temporality every day this week?

First Proof: Bodies Did Not Precede Temporal Accidents
Baqillani's first proof that bodies are temporal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's first proof that bodies are temporal because they never existed before temporal accidents.

Core Idea
Whatever coexists with or follows temporal things is itself temporal.

This lesson unpacks the first of two proofs from Imam Baqillani establishing the temporality of bodies. The logic is straightforward: bodies never existed prior to temporal accidents; they either appear with them or after them. Since accidents are created, bodies must be created as well.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the first proof in Arabic carefully. Note the key phrase 'لم تسبق الحوادث' (did not precede temporal occurrences).
This is the foundational premise.
2
Identify the two possibilities
Baqillani states that if a body does not precede accidents, it must exist either with them or after them. Both possibilities lead to the same conclusion.
The phrase 'معها أو بعدها' captures both alternatives.
3
Understand the conclusion
Since the body cannot exist independently of temporal accidents, it must itself be temporal. This is the core of the first proof.
This conclusion is necessary because the alternatives are exhaustive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليل على حدوث الأجسام أنها لم تسبق الحوادث ولم توجد قبلها وما لم يسبق المحدث محدث كهو إذ كان لا يخلو أن يكون موجوداً معه أو بعدها وكلا الأمرين يوجب حدوثه.
والدليل على أن الجسم لا يجوز أن يسبق الحوادث أنا نعلم باضطرار أنه متى كان موجوداً فلا يخلو أن يكون متماس الأبعاض مجتمعاً أو متبايناً مفترقاً لأنه ليس بين أن تكون أجزاؤه متماسة أو متباينة منزلة ثالثة فوجب ألا يصح أن يسبق الحوادث وما لم يسبق الحوادث فواجب كونه محدثاً إذ كان لا بد أن يكون إنما وجد مع وجودها أو بعدها.
The proof of the creation of bodies is that they did not precede temporal occurrences and did not exist before them, and whatever does not precede what is temporal is itself temporal, since it cannot but be existing with it or after it—both alternatives necessitate its creation. And the proof that a body cannot precede temporal occurrences is that we know by necessity that whenever it exists, it is either coherent in its parts, joined together, or separated, disjointed, because there is no third state between its parts being contiguous or separate. Thus it is necessary that it be incorrect for it to precede temporal occurrences, and whatever does not precede temporal occurrences must necessarily be created, since it must have come into existence either with them or after them.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage provides two arguments for the creation of bodies. The first argument: bodies never precede temporal accidents—they always coexist with them or come after them. Since the accidents are temporal, the bodies that accompany them must also be temporal. The second argument: a body always has a configuration—its parts are either contiguous or separated. These configurations are accidents that are not essential to the body, and they are temporal because they change. Since the body cannot be stripped of these temporal states, it must itself be temporal. The argument proceeds by eliminating the possibility that the body could exist before any accident, concluding that it must come into existence simultaneously with or after the accidents.

Key Terms
جسم
حادث
سبق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, why must bodies be temporal?
A) Because they precede temporal accidents
B) Because they cannot exist without temporal accidents, either coexisting or following them
C) Because they are made of atoms
D) Because they are eternal

Key Takeaway
The first proof shows that bodies must be temporal because they are inseparable from temporal accidents: they either appear simultaneously with them or come after them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof shows that your own body is temporal, coming into existence with and dependent on temporary accidents. Do you truly feel your complete dependence on Allah every moment, or do you sometimes act as if you are self-sufficient? Write one specific action you will take tomorrow to remind yourself of your contingency.
?
If bodies cannot precede temporal occurrences, then the world is not eternal. How does this reality challenge your everyday attachments to worldly things? What should change in your priorities given that everything around you is temporary?
?
The argument forces you to conclude that you are a created being, not an independent entity. How does this reshape your understanding of accountability to the Creator? Are you living as if you will be held responsible for your use of this temporary body?

Second Proof: Bodies Always Possess a Spatial Configuration
Baqillani's second proof based on spatial configuration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's second proof that a body's necessary spatial configuration (contiguous or separated) demonstrates its temporality.

Core Idea
A body always has a spatial state, and that state is a temporal accident.

Baqillani's second proof focuses on the inherent nature of bodies: they always have their parts either joined together or separated. This spatial configuration is an accident that changes, making it temporal. Since the body cannot be stripped of this accident, it must itself be temporal.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the second proof in Arabic. Note the exhaustive division: either the parts are contiguous (متماسة) or separated (متباينة).
There is no third state between these two.
2
Understand the implication of the division
Since the body must always be in one of these two states, and both states are accidents (they change), the body is always accompanied by a temporal accident.
This is established by necessity (بالاضطرار).
3
Draw the conclusion
Because the body cannot exist without a temporal accident, it cannot precede temporal occurrences and must itself be temporal.
The argument mirrors the first proof but adds a deeper explanation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليل على حدوث الأجسام أنها لم تسبق الحوادث ولم توجد قبلها وما لم يسبق المحدث محدث كهو إذ كان لا يخلو أن يكون موجوداً معه أو بعدها وكلا الأمرين يوجب حدوثه.
والدليل على أن الجسم لا يجوز أن يسبق الحوادث أنا نعلم باضطرار أنه متى كان موجوداً فلا يخلو أن يكون متماس الأبعاض مجتمعاً أو متبايناً مفترقاً لأنه ليس بين أن تكون أجزاؤه متماسة أو متباينة منزلة ثالثة فوجب ألا يصح أن يسبق الحوادث وما لم يسبق الحوادث فواجب كونه محدثاً إذ كان لا بد أن يكون إنما وجد مع وجودها أو بعدها.
The proof of the creation of bodies is that they did not precede temporal occurrences and did not exist before them, and whatever does not precede what is temporal is itself temporal, since it cannot but be existing with it or after it—both alternatives necessitate its creation. And the proof that a body cannot precede temporal occurrences is that we know by necessity that whenever it exists, it is either coherent in its parts, joined together, or separated, disjointed, because there is no third state between its parts being contiguous or separate. Thus it is necessary that it be incorrect for it to precede temporal occurrences, and whatever does not precede temporal occurrences must necessarily be created, since it must have come into existence either with them or after them.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage provides two arguments for the creation of bodies. The first argument: bodies never precede temporal accidents—they always coexist with them or come after them. Since the accidents are temporal, the bodies that accompany them must also be temporal. The second argument: a body always has a configuration—its parts are either contiguous or separated. These configurations are accidents that are not essential to the body, and they are temporal because they change. Since the body cannot be stripped of these temporal states, it must itself be temporal. The argument proceeds by eliminating the possibility that the body could exist before any accident, concluding that it must come into existence simultaneously with or after the accidents.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument assumes that bodies cannot exist without any accident at all, but it is actually about the impossibility of existing without a spatial configuration.
Correction: The argument does not claim that bodies require every kind of accident; it only asserts that a body must always have a spatial configuration (contiguous or separated), which is an accident.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The argument concludes that whatever does not precede temporal occurrences must be created. Since you know your body is temporal, what does that demand of you regarding your relationship with the Eternal Creator? Are you acting on that demand today?
?

The Impossibility of Traversing an Infinite Past
Baqillani's traversal argument against an infinite past

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why an infinite temporal series cannot be traversed to reach the present moment, and why this proves the world had a beginning.

Core Idea
Infinite past cannot be traversed, so the world must have begun.

Imam al-Baqillani presents a powerful rational argument against an infinite past. He asks: how could we ever reach the present if the past had no beginning? The very idea of completing an infinite sequence is self-contradictory. In this lesson, we examine the traversal argument and its implications for the creation of the world.

Guided Path
1
Read the traversal argument
Read the Arabic passage carefully. It describes the impossibility of traversing an infinite series of past events to reach the present.
2
Understand the logic
Notice that if the past were infinite, the present could never arrive because each event would have an infinite number of predecessors.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
3
Connect to the conclusion
Since the present exists, the past cannot be infinite; therefore the world had a first temporal occurrence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأقول أيضاً كيف يمكنني قطع ما لا بداية في جانب الماضي من الخطوات مثلاً للوصول إلى المكان المرام فمعنى ذلك أنه لم يحصل مني وصول لأن ما لا أول له من الحوادث لا تنتهي النوبة إلى وجود الحادث الحاضر في الحال. وانقضاء ما لا نهاية له محال لأنك إذا لاحظت الحادث الحاضر ثم انتقلت إلى ما قبله وهلم جرا على الترتيب لم تفض إلى نهاية. ووجود ما لا نهاية له من الحوادث محال وإن لم يمكن عدم إفضائك إلى نهاية لكان لتلك الحوادث أول.
وعندنا دليل عقلي بعبارة أخرى فنقول: لو كان أفراد العالم التي دخلت في الوجود لا نهاية لها لكان لا يخلو عددها عن أن يكون زوجاً أو فرداً معاً أو لا زوجاً ولا فرداً ومحال أن يكون زوجاً وفرداً جميعاً ولا زوجاً ولا فرداً فإن في ذلك جمعاً بين النفي والإثبات وهما ضدان إذ في إثبات أحدهما نفي الآخر وفي نفي أحدهما إثبات الآخر ومحال أن يكون زوجاً فقط لأن الزوج يكون فرداً بزيادة واحد فيكون يعوز ما لا نهاية له واحد ومحال أن يكون فرداً فقط لأن الفرد يكون زوجاً بزيادة واحد عليه فكيف يعوز واحد ما لا نهاية له فحصل من هذا أن العالم لا يخلو من الحوادث فهو إذاً حادث وإلا لزم استحالة وجود الحادث الحاضر لأنه لزم وجود حوادث لا أول لها فلانتفاء وجود حوادث لا أول لها انتفى ملزومه وهو كون ما لا يخلو من الحوادث قديماً، فثبت نقيضه وهو ما لا يخلو من الحوادث حادث فتبين وجود انتهاء الحوادث التي دخلت في الوجود إلى أول.
I also say: how can I traverse what has no beginning in the past, for example, steps to reach the desired place? That means that I have not reached because what has no first among temporal occurrences does not have the turn come to the present temporal occurrence in the present moment. And the ending of what is infinite is impossible because if you observe the present event and then move back to what preceded it and so on in order, you do not reach an end. And the existence of an infinite number of temporal occurrences is impossible, and if it were not impossible for you to not reach an end, then those events would have a beginning. And we have another rational proof: if the individuals of the world that have come into existence were infinite, then their number would either be even or odd or both or neither, but it is impossible for it to be both even and odd or neither, because that would combine negation and affirmation, which are opposites. And it is impossible for it to be only even because an even becomes odd by adding one, so an infinite would lack one, which is impossible. And it is impossible for it to be only odd because odd becomes even by adding one, so how can an infinite lack one? From this it follows that the world is not free from temporal occurrences, therefore it is created. Otherwise the present event's existence would be impossible because it would require an infinite chain of events with no beginning. Since the existence of events with no beginning is impossible, its entailment is also negated, namely that what is not free from events is eternal. So its opposite is proven: what is not free from events is created, thus the events that have occurred have a first.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage contains two rational proofs for the creation of the world based on the impossibility of an infinite past. The first proof is the 'traversal argument': to reach the present moment, an infinite series of past events would need to be traversed, which is impossible because an infinite cannot be completed. The second proof is the 'even-odd argument': if the past were infinite, the number of events would be either even or odd. But an infinite set cannot be assigned an even or odd number because adding or subtracting one would not change its infinitude, yet parity arguments lead to contradictions. Therefore, the past must be finite, meaning the world had a beginning. Both arguments conclude that the world is temporally originated (ḥādith).

Key Terms
لا نهاية
قدم
محال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the traversal argument depends on our ability to physically travel through time.
Correction: The argument is conceptual: it is about the logical impossibility of an infinite series being completed, not about physical traversal.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what is impossible regarding the past if it were infinite?
A) We could not count all past events
B) The present moment could never be reached
C) We could not remember past events
D) The universe would be eternal

Key Takeaway
The traversal argument shows that an infinite past is impossible because the present moment could not be reached, proving the world had a beginning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are reading this at a specific moment in time. Baqillani’s argument says that this moment could only exist if the past had a beginning. Do you truly live with the awareness that your existence is a direct gift from a Creator who brought everything into being from nothing? If you did, what would change in how you spend your next hour?
?
If an infinite past is impossible, then every moment is finite and precious. Are there things you keep postponing as if time is endless? How does the realization that the past had a beginning—and that this moment is a unique point in a finite series—urge you to act now on what matters most for your eternal life?
?
The argument shows that the present moment could not occur if the past were infinite. Your very existence is proof that the world began. Does this truth humble you? Or do you still live as if this world is self-sufficient and eternal? What concrete step can you take today to acknowledge that your life is entirely dependent on the One who started it all?

The Even-Odd Paradox and the Finitude of the Past
Baqillani's even-odd parity proof against infinite past

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the even-odd parity argument demonstrates that the number of past events must be finite, proving the world is created.

Core Idea
Infinite past leads to parity contradiction, so past must be finite.

Imam al-Baqillani offers a second rational proof, often called the 'even-odd argument'. If the number of past events were infinite, it would have to be either even or odd, but both lead to contradictions because adding or subtracting one from infinity does not change its quantity. This logical impossibility forces us to conclude that the number of past events is finite, meaning the world had a beginning.

Guided Path
1
Read the even-odd argument
Read the Arabic passage. Baqillani presents a logical classification: infinite number must be even, odd, both, or neither.
2
Analyze the contradictions
Notice that each possibility leads to a contradiction when considering the properties of even and odd numbers.
Even becomes odd by adding one; odd becomes even by adding one.
3
Draw the conclusion
Since none of the possibilities are tenable, an infinite number of past events is impossible. Therefore, the past is finite.

Source Text
